# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes Audit Log Middleware and Backend

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that implement API server audit logging: the audit event creation from requests, the audit policy evaluation, the audit backend dispatch (log file vs webhook), and the audit truncation for large request/response bodies.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the platform domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive analysis of the Kubernetes API server audit logging implementation. The findings have been saved to `/workspace/answer.json`.

## Summary

I found **25 Go source files** across kubernetes/kubernetes that implement the complete audit logging system:

### Core Components:
1. **Audit Event Creation** - `context.go`, `request.go` handle event creation and metadata capture
2. **Policy Evaluation** - `policy/checker.go` evaluates which events to audit based on configurable rules
3. **Backend Dispatch** - `union.go` combines multiple backends:
   - **Log Backend** - writes to files with rotation support
   - **Webhook Backend** - sends events to HTTP endpoints with retry logic
4. **Buffering** - `buffered.go` batches events with configurable size and timing
5. **Truncation** - `truncate.go` limits event and batch sizes for large payloads

### Key Processing Chain:
The request flows through `WithAudit` filter → policy evaluation → event creation → multi-stage processing (RequestReceived, ResponseStarted, ResponseComplete) → Union backend → optional Truncate wrapper → optional Buffered wrapper → final Log/Webhook backends.

### Advanced Features:
- Multi-stage event capture (request, response, panic)
- Audit annotations for custom metadata
- Configurable truncation thresholds (MaxEventSize, MaxBatchSize)
- Optional batching with throttling for webhooks
- Graceful shutdown ensuring no events are dropped
- Admission webhook integration for audit preservation

The answer includes the execution chain showing how events flow through the system and detailed documentation of all major components and their interactions.

When\n153: // b.stopCh is closed, processIncomingEvents stops and closes the buffer.\n154: func (b *bufferedBackend) processIncomingEvents(stopCh <-chan struct{}) {\n155: \tdefer close(b.buffer)\n156: \n157: \tvar (\n158: \t\tmaxWaitChan  <-chan time.Time\n159: \t\tmaxWaitTimer *time.Timer\n160: \t)\n161: \t// Only use max wait batching if batching is enabled.\n162: \tif b.maxBatchSize > 1 {\n163: \t\tmaxWaitTimer = time.NewTimer(b.maxBatchWait)\n164: \t\tmaxWaitChan = maxWaitTimer.C\n165: \t\tdefer maxWaitTimer.Stop()\n166: \t}\n167: \n168: \tfor {\n169: \t\tfunc() {\n170: \t\t\t// Recover from any panics caused by this function so a panic in the\n171: \t\t\t// goroutine can't bring down the main routine.\n172: \t\t\tdefer runtime.HandleCrash()\n173: \n174: \t\t\tif b.maxBatchSize > 1 {\n175: \t\t\t\tmaxWaitTimer.Reset(b.maxBatchWait)\n176: \t\t\t}\n177: \t\t\tb.processEvents(b.collectEvents(maxWaitChan, stopCh))\n178: \t\t}()\n179: \n180: \t\tselect {\n181: \t\tcase <-stopCh:\n182: \t\t\treturn\n183: \t\tdefault:\n184: \t\t}\n185: \t}\n186: }\n187: \n188: // collectEvents attempts to collect some number of events in a batch.\n189: //\n190: // The following things can cause collectEvents to stop and return the list\n191: // of events:\n192: //\n193: //   - Maximum number of events for a batch.\n194: //   - Timer has passed.\n195: //   - Buffer channel is closed and empty.\n196: //   - stopCh is closed.\n197: func (b *bufferedBackend) collectEvents(timer <-chan time.Time, stopCh <-chan struct{}) []*auditinternal.Event {\n198: \tvar events []*auditinternal.Event\n199: \n200: L:\n201: \tfor i := 0; i < b.maxBatchSize; i++ {\n202: \t\tselect {\n203: \t\tcase ev, ok := <-b.buffer:\n204: \t\t\t// Buffer channel was closed and no new events will follow.\n205: \t\t\tif !ok {\n206: \t\t\t\tbreak L\n207: \t\t\t}\n208: \t\t\tevents = append(events, ev)\n209: \t\tcase <-timer:\n210: \t\t\t// Timer has expired. Send currently accumulated batch.\n211: \t\t\tbreak L\n212: \t\tcase <-stopCh:\n213: \t\t\t// Backend has been stopped. Send currently accumulated batch.\n214: \t\t\tbreak L\n215: \t\t}\n216: \t}\n217: \n218: \treturn events\n219: }\n220: \n221: // processEvents process the batch events in a goroutine using delegateBackend's ProcessEvents.\n222: func (b *bufferedBackend) processEvents(events []*auditinternal.Event) {\n223: \tif len(events) == 0 {\n224: \t\treturn\n225: \t}\n226: \n227: \t// TODO(audit): Should control the number of active goroutines\n228: \t// if one goroutine takes 5 seconds to finish, the number of goroutines can be 5 * defaultBatchThrottleQPS\n229: \tif b.throttle != nil {\n230: \t\tb.throttle.Accept()\n231: \t}\n232: \n233: \tif b.asyncDelegate {\n234: \t\tb.wg.Add(1)\n235: \t\tgo func() {\n236: \t\t\tdefer b.wg.Done()\n237: \t\t\tdefer runtime.HandleCrash()\n238: \n239: \t\t\t// Execute the real processing in a goroutine to keep it from blocking.\n240: \t\t\t// This lets the batching routine continue draining the queue immediately.\n241: \t\t\tb.delegateBackend.ProcessEvents(events...)\n242: \t\t}()\n243: \t} else {\n244: \t\tfunc() {\n245: \t\t\tdefer runtime.HandleCrash()\n246: \n247: \t\t\t// Execute the real processing in a goroutine to keep it from blocking.\n248: \t\t\t// This lets the batching routine continue draining the queue immediately.\n249: \t\t\tb.delegateBackend.ProcessEvents(events...)\n250: \t\t}()\n251: \t}\n252: }\n253: \n254: func (b *bufferedBackend) ProcessEvents(ev ...*auditinternal.Event) bool {\n255: \t// The following mechanism is in place to support the situation when audit\n256: \t// events are still coming after the backend was stopped.\n257: \tvar sendErr error\n258: \tvar evIndex int\n259: \n260: \t// If the delegateBackend was shutdown and the buffer channel was closed, an\n261: \t// attempt to add an event to it will result in panic that we should\n262: \t// recover from.\n263: \tdefer func() {\n264: \t\tif err := recover(); err != nil {\n265: \t\t\tsendErr = fmt.Errorf(\"audit backend shut down\")\n266: \t\t}\n267: \t\tif sendErr != nil {\n268: \t\t\taudit.HandlePluginError(PluginName, sendErr, ev[evIndex:]...)\n269: \t\t}\n270: \t}()\n271: \n272: \tfor i, e := range ev {\n273: \t\tevIndex = i\n274: \t\t// Per the audit.Backend interface these events are reused after being\n275: \t\t// sent to the Sink. Deep copy and send the copy to the queue.\n276: \t\tevent := e.DeepCopy()\n277: \n278: \t\tselect {\n279: \t\tcase b.buffer <- event:\n280: \t\tdefault:\n281: \t\t\tsendErr = fmt.Errorf(\"audit buffer queue blocked\")\n282: \t\t\treturn true\n283: \t\t}\n284: \t}\n285: \treturn true\n286: }\n287: \n288: func (b *bufferedBackend) String() string {\n289: \treturn fmt.Sprintf(\"%s<%s>\", PluginName, b.delegateBackend)\n290: }\n291: ",

Kubernetes API server implements comprehensive audit logging that captures API requests and responses through a pipeline that includes audit event creation, policy evaluation, backend dispatch, and optional truncation for large payloads.\\n\\n## Key Components\\n\\n### 1. Audit Event Creation and Context Management\\n\\n**Types and Interfaces** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/types.go`):\\n- Defines the `Backend` interface that all audit backends must implement\\n- Defines the `Sink` interface for processing events\\n- Backend must support `ProcessEvents()`, `Run()`, `Shutdown()`, and `String()` methods\\n\\n**Audit Context** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/context.go`):\\n- `AuditContext` holds the audit event data and configuration for a single request\\n- `WithAuditContext()` creates a new context with an AuditContext\\n- `AuditContextFrom()` retrieves the AuditContext from a request context\\n- `ProcessEventStage()` sends the event to the audit sink at different stages (RequestReceived, ResponseStarted, ResponseComplete, Panic)\\n- Audit annotations can be added via `AddAuditAnnotation()` and related functions\\n\\n**Request Logging** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/request.go`):\\n- `LogRequestMetadata()` populates request metadata (verb, user, source IP, etc.)\\n- `LogRequestObject()` encodes and logs the request body\\n- `LogResponseObject()` encodes and logs the response body\\n- Functions handle managed fields removal and object encoding\\n\\n### 2. Audit Policy Evaluation\\n\\n**Policy Evaluator Interface** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/evaluator.go`):\\n- `PolicyRuleEvaluator` interface evaluates audit policy rules against request attributes\\n- `RequestAuditConfig` holds the evaluated audit level (None, Metadata, Request, RequestResponse) and omit stages\\n\\n**Policy Checker** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/policy/checker.go`):\\n- `NewPolicyRuleEvaluator()` creates an evaluator from an audit policy\\n- `EvaluatePolicyRule()` matches request attributes against policy rules\\n- Supports matching by users, groups, verbs, resources, namespaces, and non-resource URLs\\n- Rules can specify which stages to omit and whether to omit managed fields\\n\\n**Policy Loading** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/policy/reader.go`):\\n- Loads and parses audit policy files\\n- Validates policy format and rules\\n\\n### 3. Audit Event Stages and Middleware\\n\\n**Main Audit Filter** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/audit.go`):\\n- `WithAudit()` is the primary middleware that wraps the HTTP handler\\n- `evaluatePolicyAndCreateAuditEvent()` evaluates policy and initializes audit context\\n- Events are sent at multiple stages:\\n  - `StageRequestReceived` - when request arrives\\n  - `StageResponseStarted` - when response headers are set\\n  - `StageResponseComplete` - when response is complete\\n  - `StagePanic` - if handler panics\\n\\n**Audit Initialization** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/audit_init.go`):\\n- `WithAuditInit()` initializes the audit context and audit ID\\n- Generates or retrieves the Audit-ID from request headers\\n- Echoes the Audit-ID in response headers\\n\\n**Failed Authentication Audit** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authn_audit.go`):\\n- `WithFailedAuthenticationAudit()` audits failed authentication attempts\\n\\n### 4. Backend Dispatch and Implementations\\n\\n**Union Backend** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/union.go`):\\n- `Union()` combines multiple backends to send events to all of them\\n- Processes events sequentially through all backends\\n\\n**Log Backend** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/log/backend.go`):\\n- Writes audit events to a file\\n- Supports legacy text format and JSON format\\n- `ProcessEvents()` encodes events and writes them to the output stream\\n\\n**Webhook Backend** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/webhook/webhook.go`):\\n- Sends audit events to an HTTP webhook endpoint\\n- `ProcessEvents()` creates an EventList and POSTs to the webhook\\n- Supports retry with exponential backoff\\n- Can be configured from kubeconfig file or REST client\\n\\n**Buffered/Batching Backend** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/buffered/buffered.go`):\\n- Batches audit events before sending to a delegate backend\\n- Configurable buffer size, max batch size, and max wait time\\n- Supports three modes:\\n  - `ModeBatch` - buffers events and sends batches asynchronously\\n  - `ModeBlocking` - blocks request processing until events are sent\\n  - `ModeBlockingStrict` - blocks and fails request on audit errors\\n- Optional throttling with QPS and burst limits\\n- `Run()` starts goroutines to process incoming events\\n- `Shutdown()` waits for all events to be processed\\n\\n### 5. Audit Truncation for Large Payloads\\n\\n**Truncate Backend** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/truncate/truncate.go`):\\n- Wraps another backend to limit event and batch sizes\\n- `Config` specifies `MaxEventSize` and `MaxBatchSize`\\n- `ProcessEvents()` truncates events by removing request/response objects if they exceed size limits\\n- Splits large batches into smaller ones\\n- Adds truncation annotation when events are truncated\\n- Dropped events that still exceed limits after truncation generate errors\\n\\n### 6. Configuration and Backend Assembly\\n\\n**Audit Options** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/options/audit.go`):\\n- `AuditOptions` holds policy file path\\n- `AuditLogOptions` configures file-based logging with rotation\\n- `AuditWebhookOptions` configures webhook endpoints\\n- `AuditBatchOptions` configures batching behavior\\n- `AuditTruncateOptions` configures truncation\\n- `ApplyTo()` assembles the complete backend pipeline:\\n  1. Load audit policy\\n  2. Create log backend (if enabled)\\n  3. Create webhook backend (if enabled)\\n  4. Wrap webhook backend with truncation\\n  5. Combine log and webhook backends using Union\\n  6. Set policy evaluator and backend on server config\\n\\n**Backend Assembly Pattern**:\\n- Log backend: `log backend -> batch wrapper -> truncate wrapper`\\n- Webhook backend: `webhook backend -> batch wrapper -> truncate wrapper`\\n- Final: `Union(log backend, webhook backend)` or individual backends\\n\\n### 7. Request Handler Integration\\n\\n**Handler Audit Calls** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/`):\\n- `create.go`: calls `LogRequestObject()` for create operations\\n- `update.go`: calls `LogRequestObject()` and wraps admission with `admission.WithAudit()`\\n- `delete.go`: calls `AddAuditAnnotation()` for unsafe delete flags\\n\\n**Admission Integration** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/audit.go`):\\n- `WithAudit()` decorator preserves audit annotations from admission webhooks\\n\\n### 8. Server Integration\\n\\n**Generic API Server** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/genericapiserver.go`):\\n- `AuditBackend` field holds the configured audit backend\\n- `Run()` starts the audit backend before the server starts listening\\n- `Shutdown()` gracefully shuts down the audit backend\\n\\n## Event Flow\\n\\n1. **Request Arrives**: `WithAuditInit` generates or retrieves Audit-ID\\n2. **WithAudit Filter**: Evaluates policy against request attributes\\n3. **StageRequestReceived**: Event sent to sink with request metadata\\n4. **Request Processing**: Handlers may add audit annotations\\n5. **Response Generated**: StageResponseStarted and StageResponseComplete events sent\\n6. **Backend Processing**:\\n   - Union backend sends to all configured backends\\n   - Truncate backend (if enabled) may truncate large events\\n   - Buffered backend (if enabled) batches events\\n   - Log or Webhook backend processes final events\\n\\n## Key Features\\n\\n- **Policy-driven**: Events are filtered and leveled based on configurable policy rules\\n- **Multi-stage**: Captures request received, response started, response complete, and panic stages\\n- **Multiple backends**: Can simultaneously write to files and webhooks\\n- **Batching**: Optional batching of events to webhooks with configurable batch size and timing\\n- **Truncation**: Optional size-limiting of events and batches for large request/response bodies\\n- **Asynchronous processing**: Log files use synchronous writes, webhooks use asynchronous batching\\n- **Graceful shutdown**: Ensures all in-flight events are processed before shutdown\\n- **Annotations**: Supports adding custom audit annotations at various request stages\\n\"\n}\nEOF\ncat /workspace/answer.json\n"

Kubernetes API server implements comprehensive audit logging that captures API requests and responses through a pipeline that includes audit event creation, policy evaluation, backend dispatch, and optional truncation for large payloads.\\n\\n## Key Components\\n\\n### 1. Audit Event Creation and Context Management\\n\\n**Types and Interfaces** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/types.go`):\\n- Defines the `Backend` interface that all audit backends must implement\\n- Defines the `Sink` interface for processing events\\n- Backend must support `ProcessEvents()`, `Run()`, `Shutdown()`, and `String()` methods\\n\\n**Audit Context** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/context.go`):\\n- `AuditContext` holds the audit event data and configuration for a single request\\n- `WithAuditContext()` creates a new context with an AuditContext\\n- `AuditContextFrom()` retrieves the AuditContext from a request context\\n- `ProcessEventStage()` sends the event to the audit sink at different stages (RequestReceived, ResponseStarted, ResponseComplete, Panic)\\n- Audit annotations can be added via `AddAuditAnnotation()` and related functions\\n\\n**Request Logging** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/request.go`):\\n- `LogRequestMetadata()` populates request metadata (verb, user, source IP, etc.)\\n- `LogRequestObject()` encodes and logs the request body\\n- `LogResponseObject()` encodes and logs the response body\\n- Functions handle managed fields removal and object encoding\\n\\n### 2. Audit Policy Evaluation\\n\\n**Policy Evaluator Interface** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/evaluator.go`):\\n- `PolicyRuleEvaluator` interface evaluates audit policy rules against request attributes\\n- `RequestAuditConfig` holds the evaluated audit level (None, Metadata, Request, RequestResponse) and omit stages\\n\\n**Policy Checker** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/policy/checker.go`):\\n- `NewPolicyRuleEvaluator()` creates an evaluator from an audit policy\\n- `EvaluatePolicyRule()` matches request attributes against policy rules\\n- Supports matching by users, groups, verbs, resources, namespaces, and non-resource URLs\\n- Rules can specify which stages to omit and whether to omit managed fields\\n\\n**Policy Loading** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/policy/reader.go`):\\n- Loads and parses audit policy files\\n- Validates policy format and rules\\n\\n### 3. Audit Event Stages and Middleware\\n\\n**Main Audit Filter** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/audit.go`):\\n- `WithAudit()` is the primary middleware that wraps the HTTP handler\\n- `evaluatePolicyAndCreateAuditEvent()` evaluates policy and initializes audit context\\n- Events are sent at multiple stages:\\n  - `StageRequestReceived` - when request arrives\\n  - `StageResponseStarted` - when response headers are set\\n  - `StageResponseComplete` - when response is complete\\n  - `StagePanic` - if handler panics\\n\\n**Audit Initialization** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/audit_init.go`):\\n- `WithAuditInit()` initializes the audit context and audit ID\\n- Generates or retrieves the Audit-ID from request headers\\n- Echoes the Audit-ID in response headers\\n\\n**Failed Authentication Audit** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authn_audit.go`):\\n- `WithFailedAuthenticationAudit()` audits failed authentication attempts\\n\\n### 4. Backend Dispatch and Implementations\\n\\n**Union Backend** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/union.go`):\\n- `Union()` combines multiple backends to send events to all of them\\n- Processes events sequentially through all backends\\n\\n**Log Backend** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/log/backend.go`):\\n- Writes audit events to a file\\n- Supports legacy text format and JSON format\\n- `ProcessEvents()` encodes events and writes them to the output stream\\n\\n**Webhook Backend** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/webhook/webhook.go`):\\n- Sends audit events to an HTTP webhook endpoint\\n- `ProcessEvents()` creates an EventList and POSTs to the webhook\\n- Supports retry with exponential backoff\\n- Can be configured from kubeconfig file or REST client\\n\\n**Buffered/Batching Backend** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/buffered/buffered.go`):\\n- Batches audit events before sending to a delegate backend\\n- Configurable buffer size, max batch size, and max wait time\\n- Supports three modes:\\n  - `ModeBatch` - buffers events and sends batches asynchronously\\n  - `ModeBlocking` - blocks request processing until events are sent\\n  - `ModeBlockingStrict` - blocks and fails request on audit errors\\n- Optional throttling with QPS and burst limits\\n- `Run()` starts goroutines to process incoming events\\n- `Shutdown()` waits for all events to be processed\\n\\n### 5. Audit Truncation for Large Payloads\\n\\n**Truncate Backend** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/truncate/truncate.go`):\\n- Wraps another backend to limit event and batch sizes\\n- `Config` specifies `MaxEventSize` and `MaxBatchSize`\\n- `ProcessEvents()` truncates events by removing request/response objects if they exceed size limits\\n- Splits large batches into smaller ones\\n- Adds truncation annotation when events are truncated\\n- Dropped events that still exceed limits after truncation generate errors\\n\\n### 6. Configuration and Backend Assembly\\n\\n**Audit Options** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/options/audit.go`):\\n- `AuditOptions` holds policy file path\\n- `AuditLogOptions` configures file-based logging with rotation\\n- `AuditWebhookOptions` configures webhook endpoints\\n- `AuditBatchOptions` configures batching behavior\\n- `AuditTruncateOptions` configures truncation\\n- `ApplyTo()` assembles the complete backend pipeline:\\n  1. Load audit policy\\n  2. Create log backend (if enabled)\\n  3. Create webhook backend (if enabled)\\n  4. Wrap webhook backend with truncation\\n  5. Combine log and webhook backends using Union\\n  6. Set policy evaluator and backend on server config\\n\\n**Backend Assembly Pattern**:\\n- Log backend: `log backend -> batch wrapper -> truncate wrapper`\\n- Webhook backend: `webhook backend -> batch wrapper -> truncate wrapper`\\n- Final: `Union(log backend, webhook backend)` or individual backends\\n\\n### 7. Request Handler Integration\\n\\n**Handler Audit Calls** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/`):\\n- `create.go`: calls `LogRequestObject()` for create operations\\n- `update.go`: calls `LogRequestObject()` and wraps admission with `admission.WithAudit()`\\n- `delete.go`: calls `AddAuditAnnotation()` for unsafe delete flags\\n\\n**Admission Integration** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/audit.go`):\\n- `WithAudit()` decorator preserves audit annotations from admission webhooks\\n\\n### 8. Server Integration\\n\\n**Generic API Server** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/genericapiserver.go`):\\n- `AuditBackend` field holds the configured audit backend\\n- `Run()` starts the audit backend before the server starts listening\\n- `Shutdown()` gracefully shuts down the audit backend\\n\\n## Event Flow\\n\\n1. **Request Arrives**: `WithAuditInit` generates or retrieves Audit-ID\\n2. **WithAudit Filter**: Evaluates policy against request attributes\\n3. **StageRequestReceived**: Event sent to sink with request metadata\\n4. **Request Processing**: Handlers may add audit annotations\\n5. **Response Generated**: StageResponseStarted and StageResponseComplete events sent\\n6. **Backend Processing**:\\n   - Union backend sends to all configured backends\\n   - Truncate backend (if enabled) may truncate large events\\n   - Buffered backend (if enabled) batches events\\n   - Log or Webhook backend processes final events\\n\\n## Key Features\\n\\n- **Policy-driven**: Events are filtered and leveled based on configurable policy rules\\n- **Multi-stage**: Captures request received, response started, response complete, and panic stages\\n- **Multiple backends**: Can simultaneously write to files and webhooks\\n- **Batching**: Optional batching of events to webhooks with configurable batch size and timing\\n- **Truncation**: Optional size-limiting of events and batches for large request/response bodies\\n- **Asynchronous processing**: Log files use synchronous writes, webhooks use asynchronous batching\\n- **Graceful shutdown**: Ensures all in-flight events are processed before shutdown\\n- **Annotations**: Supports adding custom audit annotations at various request stages\\n\"\n}"
}

  "text": "# Kubernetes API Server Audit Logging Implementation\n\n## Overview\n\nThe Kubernetes API server implements comprehensive audit logging that captures API requests and responses through a pipeline that includes audit event creation, policy evaluation, backend dispatch, and optional truncation for large payloads.\n\n## Key Components\n\n### 1. Audit Event Creation and Context Management\n\n**Types and Interfaces** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/types.go`):\n- Defines the `Backend` interface that all audit backends must implement\n- Defines the `Sink` interface for processing events\n- Backend must support `ProcessEvents()`, `Run()`, `Shutdown()`, and `String()` methods\n\n**Audit Context** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/context.go`):\n- `AuditContext` holds the audit event data and configuration for a single request\n- `WithAuditContext()` creates a new context with an AuditContext\n- `AuditContextFrom()` retrieves the AuditContext from a request context\n- `ProcessEventStage()` sends the event to the audit sink at different stages (RequestReceived, ResponseStarted, ResponseComplete, Panic)\n- Audit annotations can be added via `AddAuditAnnotation()` and related functions\n\n**Request Logging** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/request.go`):\n- `LogRequestMetadata()` populates request metadata (verb, user, source IP, etc.)\n- `LogRequestObject()` encodes and logs the request body\n- `LogResponseObject()` encodes and logs the response body\n- Functions handle managed fields removal and object encoding\n\n### 2. Audit Policy Evaluation\n\n**Policy Evaluator Interface** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/evaluator.go`):\n- `PolicyRuleEvaluator` interface evaluates audit policy rules against request attributes\n- `RequestAuditConfig` holds the evaluated audit level (None, Metadata, Request, RequestResponse) and omit stages\n\n**Policy Checker** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/policy/checker.go`):\n- `NewPolicyRuleEvaluator()` creates an evaluator from an audit policy\n- `EvaluatePolicyRule()` matches request attributes against policy rules\n- Supports matching by users, groups, verbs, resources, namespaces, and non-resource URLs\n- Rules can specify which stages to omit and whether to omit managed fields\n\n**Policy Loading** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/policy/reader.go`):\n- Loads and parses audit policy files\n- Validates policy format and rules\n\n### 3. Audit Event Stages and Middleware\n\n**Main Audit Filter** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/audit.go`):\n- `WithAudit()` is the primary middleware that wraps the HTTP handler\n- `evaluatePolicyAndCreateAuditEvent()` evaluates policy and initializes audit context\n- Events are sent at multiple stages:\n  - `StageRequestReceived` - when request arrives\n  - `StageResponseStarted` - when response headers are set\n  - `StageResponseComplete` - when response is complete\n  - `StagePanic` - if handler panics\n\n**Audit Initialization** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/audit_init.go`):\n- `WithAuditInit()` initializes the audit context and audit ID\n- Generates or retrieves the Audit-ID from request headers\n- Echoes the Audit-ID in response headers\n\n**Failed Authentication Audit** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authn_audit.go`):\n- `WithFailedAuthenticationAudit()` audits failed authentication attempts\n\n### 4. Backend Dispatch and Implementations\n\n**Union Backend** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/union.go`):\n- `Union()` combines multiple backends to send events to all of them\n- Processes events sequentially through all backends\n\n**Log Backend** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/log/backend.go`):\n- Writes audit events to a file\n- Supports legacy text format and JSON format\n- `ProcessEvents()` encodes events and writes them to the output stream\n\n**Webhook Backend** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/webhook/webhook.go`):\n- Sends audit events to an HTTP webhook endpoint\n- `ProcessEvents()` creates an EventList and POSTs to the webhook\n- Supports retry with exponential backoff\n- Can be configured from kubeconfig file or REST client\n\n**Buffered/Batching Backend** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/buffered/buffered.go`):\n- Batches audit events before sending to a delegate backend\n- Configurable buffer size, max batch size, and max wait time\n- Supports three modes:\n  - `ModeBatch` - buffers events and sends batches asynchronously\n  - `ModeBlocking` - blocks request processing until events are sent\n  - `ModeBlockingStrict` - blocks and fails request on audit errors\n- Optional throttling with QPS and burst limits\n- `Run()` starts goroutines to process incoming events\n- `Shutdown()` waits for all events to be processed\n\n### 5. Audit Truncation for Large Payloads\n\n**Truncate Backend** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/truncate/truncate.go`):\n- Wraps another backend to limit event and batch sizes\n- `Config` specifies `MaxEventSize` and `MaxBatchSize`\n- `ProcessEvents()` truncates events by removing request/response objects if they exceed size limits\n- Splits large batches into smaller ones\n- Adds truncation annotation when events are truncated\n- Dropped events that still exceed limits after truncation generate errors\n\n### 6. Configuration and Backend Assembly\n\n**Audit Options** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/options/audit.go`):\n- `AuditOptions` holds policy file path\n- `AuditLogOptions` configures file-based logging with rotation\n- `AuditWebhookOptions` configures webhook endpoints\n- `AuditBatchOptions` configures batching behavior\n- `AuditTruncateOptions` configures truncation\n- `ApplyTo()` assembles the complete backend pipeline:\n  1. Load audit policy\n  2. Create log backend (if enabled)\n  3. Create webhook backend (if enabled)\n  4. Wrap webhook backend with truncation\n  5. Combine log and webhook backends using Union\n  6. Set policy evaluator and backend on server config\n\n**Backend Assembly Pattern**:\n- Log backend: `log backend -> batch wrapper -> truncate wrapper`\n- Webhook backend: `webhook backend -> batch wrapper -> truncate wrapper`\n- Final: `Union(log backend, webhook backend)` or individual backends\n\n### 7. Request Handler Integration\n\n**Handler Audit Calls** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/`):\n- `create.go`: calls `LogRequestObject()` for create operations\n- `update.go`: calls `LogRequestObject()` and wraps admission with `admission.WithAudit()`\n- `delete.go`: calls `AddAuditAnnotation()` for unsafe delete flags\n\n**Admission Integration** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/audit.go`):\n- `WithAudit()` decorator preserves audit annotations from admission webhooks\n\n### 8. Server Integration\n\n**Generic API Server** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/genericapiserver.go`):\n- `AuditBackend` field holds the configured audit backend\n- `Run()` starts the audit backend before the server starts listening\n- `Shutdown()` gracefully shuts down the audit backend\n\n## Event Flow\n\n1. **Request Arrives**: `WithAuditInit` generates or retrieves Audit-ID\n2. **WithAudit Filter**: Evaluates policy against request attributes\n3. **StageRequestReceived**: Event sent to sink with request metadata\n4. **Request Processing**: Handlers may add audit annotations\n5. **Response Generated**: StageResponseStarted and StageResponseComplete events sent\n6. **Backend Processing**:\n   - Union backend sends to all configured backends\n   - Truncate backend (if enabled) may truncate large events\n   - Buffered backend (if enabled) batches events\n   - Log or Webhook backend processes final events\n\n## Key Features\n\n- **Policy-driven**: Events are filtered and leveled based on configurable policy rules\n- **Multi-stage**: Captures request received, response started, response complete, and panic stages\n- **Multiple backends**: Can simultaneously write to files and webhooks\n- **Batching**: Optional batching of events to webhooks with configurable batch size and timing\n- **Truncation**: Optional size-limiting of events and batches for large request/response bodies\n- **Asynchronous processing**: Log files use synchronous writes, webhooks use asynchronous batching\n- **Graceful shutdown**: Ensures all in-flight events are processed before shutdown\n- **Annotations**: Supports adding custom audit annotations at various request stages\n"
